1:6e1c9cd: 
3:eac0369: 
2:eac0369: /**
1:eac0369: 	List of error message identifiers.
1:eac0369: 	This is the set of message identifiers. The message identifier
1:eac0369: 	also encodes the SQLState as the first five characters.
1:eac0369: 	StandardExceptions must be created using the static
1:eac0369: 	StandardException.newException() method calls, passing in a
1:eac0369: 	field from this class.
1:eac0369: 	<BR>
1:eac0369: 	The five character SQL State is obtained from a StandardException
1:eac0369: 	using the zero-argument StandardException.getSQLState() method.
1:eac0369: 	<BR>
1:eac0369: 	The message identifier (ie. the value that matches a field in this class)
1:eac0369: 	is obtained using the zero-argument StandardException.getMessageId() method.
1:eac0369: 	<BR>
1:eac0369: 	Thus if checking for a specific error using a field from this interface
1:eac0369: 	the correct code is
1:eac0369: 	<PRE>
1:eac0369: 		if (se.getMessageId().equals(SQLState.DEADLOCK))
1:eac0369: 	</PRE>
1:eac0369: 	<BR>
1:eac0369: 	A utility static method StandardException.getSQLState(String messageId)
1:eac0369: 	exists to convert an field from this class into a five character SQLState.
1:eac0369: 	<P>
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<P>
1:eac0369: 	The SQL state of an error message dictates the error's severity.
1:eac0369: 	The severity is determined from the first two characters of the
1:eac0369: 	state if the state is five characters long, otherwise the state
1:eac0369: 	is expected to be 7 characters long and the last character determines
1:eac0369: 	the state. If the state is seven characters long then only the first
1:eac0369: 	five will be seen by the error reporting code and exception.
1:eac0369: 	<BR>
1:eac0369: 	If the state is 9 characters long, the last two characters encode
1:eac0369: 	an exception category, which Synchronization uses to determine whether
1:eac0369: 	the error causes REFRESH to halt or to simply skip the failed transaction.
1:eac0369: 	All 5 and 7 character states default to the ENVIRONMENTAL exception
1:eac0369: 	category.
1:eac0369: 	<BR>
1:eac0369: 	Here is the encoding of the SQL state, broken down by severity.
1:eac0369: 	<UL>
1:eac0369: 	<LI> <B> SYSTEM_SEVERITY </B>
1:eac0369: 		xxxxx.M
1:eac0369: 		
1:eac0369: 	<LI> <B> DATABASE_SEVERITY </B>
1:eac0369: 		xxxxx.D
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI> <B> SESSION_SEVERITY </B>
1:eac0369: 	    08xxx
1:eac0369: 		xxxxx.C
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI> <B> TRANSACTION_SEVERITY </B>
1:eac0369: 		40xxx or xxxxx.T
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI> <B> STATEMENT_SEVERITY </B>
1:eac0369: 		{2,3}xxxx, 42xxx,  07xxx  or xxxxx.S
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI> <B> WARNING_SEVERITY </B>
1:eac0369: 		01xxx <EM> SQL State rules require that warnings have states starting with 01</EM>
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI> <B> NO_APPLICABLE_SEVERITY </B>
1:eac0369: 		YYxxx (YY means none of the above) or xxxxx.U
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI> <B> TRANSIENT exception category </B>
1:eac0369: 		xxxxx.Y#T (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI> <B> CONSISTENCY exception category </B>
1:eac0369: 		xxxxx.Y#C (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI> <B> ENVIRONMENTAL exception category (the default)</B>
1:eac0369: 		xxxxx.Y#E (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI> <B> WRAPPED exception category</B>
1:eac0369: 		xxxxx.Y#W (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	</UL>
1:eac0369: 	<HR>
1:eac0369: 	<P>
1:eac0369: 	<B>SQL State ranges</B>
1:eac0369: 	<UL>
1:eac0369: 	<LI>Basic Services
1:eac0369: 	  <UL>
1:eac0369: 	  <LI> XBCA CacheService
1:eac0369: 	  <LI> XBCM ClassManager
1:eac0369: 	  <LI> XBCX	Cryptography
1:eac0369: 	  <LI> XBM0	Monitor
1:25c1e7b: 	  <LI> XBDA Communications
1:eac0369: 	  <LI> XCY0 Properties
1:eac0369: 	  </UL>
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI>Connectivity
1:eac0369: 	  <UL>
1:eac0369: 	  <LI> 08XXX Connection Exceptions
1:eac0369: 	  </UL>
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI>Language
1:eac0369: 	  <UL>
1:e185894: 		<LI> 2200J-2200R for SQL/XML errors (based on SQL/XML[2006]) </LI>
1:eac0369: 		<LI> 42800-? for compatible DB2 errors
1:eac0369: 		<LI> 42X00-42Zxx for compilation errors </LI>
1:eac0369: 		<LI> 43X00-43Yxx  for org.apache.derby.impl.sql.execute.rts
1:eac0369: 		<LI> 44X00  for all other org.apache.derby.catalog.types
1:eac0369: 		<LI> 46000  for SQLJ errors (for now, leave this range empty) </LI>
1:eac0369: 		<LI> 38000  SQL3 ranges  </LI>
1:eac0369: 		<LI> XD00x  Dependency mgr </LI>
1:f78ff52: 		<LI> XMLxx  Misc XML errors not covered by SQL standard </LI>
1:eac0369: 	  <LI> 
1:eac0369: 	  </UL>
1:eac0369: 
1:eac0369: 	<LI>Store
1:eac0369: 	  <UL>
1:eac0369: 	  <LI> XSCG0 Conglomerate
1:eac0369: 	  <LI> XSCH0 Heap
1:eac0369: 	  </UL>
1:eac0369: 
1:59a5a70: 	<LI>Security
1:59a5a70: 	  <UL>
1:59a5a70: 	  <LI> XK...
1:59a5a70: 	  </UL>
1:59a5a70: 
1:1c08813:     <LI>Replication
1:1c08813:       <UL>
1:1c08813:       <LI> XRExx
1:1c08813:       </UL>
1:1c08813: 
1:eac0369:     <LI>Reserved for IBM Use: XQC00 - XQCZZ
1:eac0369: 	</UL>
1:eac0369: */
1:eac0369:

1:eac0369: 	/*
1:eac0369: 	** Language
1:eac0369: 	**
1:eac0369: 	** The entries in this file are sorted into groups.  Add your entry
1:eac0369: 	** to the appropriate group. Language errors are divided into 3 groups:
1:eac0369: 	** A group for standard SQLExceptions.
1:eac0369: 	**
1:e185894: 	** 2200J-00R - For SQL/XML errors (based on SQL/XML[2006]).
1:8f3b0b9: 	** 4250x - access rule violations
1:eac0369: 	** 428?? - adding some DB2 compatible errors
1:eac0369: 	** 42X00-42Zxx for compilation errors 
1:eac0369: 	** 46000  for SQLJ errors (for now, leave this range empty)
1:eac0369: 	** 38000  SQL3 ranges 
1:eac0369: 	** 39001  SQL3
1:eac0369: 	** X0X00-X0Xxx for implementation-defined execution errors.
1:eac0369: 	**
1:eac0369: 	** NOTE: If an error can occur during both compilation and execution, then
1:eac0369: 	** you need 2 different errors.  
1:eac0369: 	**
1:eac0369: 	** In addition to the above groups, this file also contains SQLStates
1:eac0369: 	** for language transaction severity errors. These are in the range
1:eac0369: 	**
1:eac0369: 	**	40XC0 - 40XCZ
1:eac0369: 	**
1:eac0369: 	** implementation-defined range reserved for class 23 is L01-LZZ
1:eac0369: 	**
1:eac0369: 	**
1:eac0369: 	** Errors that have standard SQLStates
1:eac0369: 	**
1:eac0369: 	** Implementation-defined subclasses must begin with a digit from 5 through 9,
1:eac0369: 	** or a letter from I through Z (capitals only).
1:eac0369: 	**
1:eac0369:  	*/
1:eac0369:

/////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
1:     // SQLState 8006. DERBY-3077. 
commit:137e3a1
/////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
1:     String DRDA_CONNECTION_TERMINATED                           = "08006.C";
1:    
1:     // Use this version of SOCKET_EXCEPTION any time *except* when trying to
1:     // establish a connection, as the SQLState is different.  When trying
1:     // to establish a connection, use CONNECT_SOCKET_EXCEPTION.
1:     String SOCKET_EXCEPTION                                     = "08006.C.2";
1:     String COMMUNICATION_ERROR                                  = "08006.C.3";
1:     String CONNECTION_FAILED_ON_DEFERRED_RESET                  = "08006.C.4";
1:     String NET_INSUFFICIENT_DATA                                = "08006.C.5";
1:     String NET_LOB_DATA_TOO_LARGE_FOR_JVM                       = "08006.C.6";
1:   
/////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
1:     // 58009 means connection is terminated by a DRDA-protocol error.  This can be caused by any number
1:     // of reasons, so this SQL State has a lot of instances. Exceptions that are 
1:     // not protocol related, e.g. SocketException, IOException etc should use 
0:     // SQLState 8006. DERBY-3077.  The exceptions that have been moved have been
0:     // marked with an XX_MOVED_TO_8006 prefix.  Since only english has been 
0:     // changed, these should not be reused, to avoid conflicts with localized
0:     // messages.
0:     String XX_MOVED_TO_8006_DRDA_CONNECTION_TERMINATED                               = "58009.C";
0:     String XX_MOVED_TO_8006_SOCKET_EXCEPTION                                         = "58009.C.2";
0:     String XX_MOVED_TO_8006_COMMUNICATION_ERROR                                      = "58009.C.3";

commit:eac0369
/////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
1: /*
1: 
0:    Licensed Materials - Property of IBM
0:    Cloudscape - Package org.apache.derby.iapi.reference
0:    (C) Copyright IBM Corp. 1999, 2004. All Rights Reserved.
0:    US Government Users Restricted Rights - Use, duplication or
0:    disclosure restricted by GSA ADP Schedule Contract with IBM Corp.
1: 
1:  */
1: 
0: package org.apache.derby.iapi.reference;
1: 
1: 
1: /**
1: 	List of error message identifiers.
1: 	This is the set of message identifiers. The message identifier
1: 	also encodes the SQLState as the first five characters.
1: 	StandardExceptions must be created using the static
1: 	StandardException.newException() method calls, passing in a
1: 	field from this class.
1: 	<BR>
1: 	The five character SQL State is obtained from a StandardException
1: 	using the zero-argument StandardException.getSQLState() method.
1: 	<BR>
1: 	The message identifier (ie. the value that matches a field in this class)
1: 	is obtained using the zero-argument StandardException.getMessageId() method.
1: 	<BR>
1: 	Thus if checking for a specific error using a field from this interface
1: 	the correct code is
1: 	<PRE>
1: 		if (se.getMessageId().equals(SQLState.DEADLOCK))
1: 	</PRE>
1: 	<BR>
1: 	A utility static method StandardException.getSQLState(String messageId)
1: 	exists to convert an field from this class into a five character SQLState.
1: 	<P>
1: 
1: 	<P>
1: 	The SQL state of an error message dictates the error's severity.
1: 	The severity is determined from the first two characters of the
1: 	state if the state is five characters long, otherwise the state
1: 	is expected to be 7 characters long and the last character determines
1: 	the state. If the state is seven characters long then only the first
1: 	five will be seen by the error reporting code and exception.
1: 	<BR>
1: 	If the state is 9 characters long, the last two characters encode
1: 	an exception category, which Synchronization uses to determine whether
1: 	the error causes REFRESH to halt or to simply skip the failed transaction.
1: 	All 5 and 7 character states default to the ENVIRONMENTAL exception
1: 	category.
1: 	<BR>
1: 	Here is the encoding of the SQL state, broken down by severity.
1: 	<UL>
1: 	<LI> <B> SYSTEM_SEVERITY </B>
1: 		xxxxx.M
1: 		
1: 	<LI> <B> DATABASE_SEVERITY </B>
1: 		xxxxx.D
1: 
1: 	<LI> <B> SESSION_SEVERITY </B>
1: 	    08xxx
1: 		xxxxx.C
1: 
1: 	<LI> <B> TRANSACTION_SEVERITY </B>
1: 		40xxx or xxxxx.T
1: 
1: 	<LI> <B> STATEMENT_SEVERITY </B>
1: 		{2,3}xxxx, 42xxx,  07xxx  or xxxxx.S
1: 
1: 	<LI> <B> WARNING_SEVERITY </B>
1: 		01xxx <EM> SQL State rules require that warnings have states starting with 01</EM>
1: 
1: 	<LI> <B> NO_APPLICABLE_SEVERITY </B>
1: 		YYxxx (YY means none of the above) or xxxxx.U
1: 
1: 	<LI> <B> TRANSIENT exception category </B>
1: 		xxxxx.Y#T (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
1: 
1: 	<LI> <B> CONSISTENCY exception category </B>
1: 		xxxxx.Y#C (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
1: 
1: 	<LI> <B> ENVIRONMENTAL exception category (the default)</B>
1: 		xxxxx.Y#E (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
1: 
1: 	<LI> <B> WRAPPED exception category</B>
1: 		xxxxx.Y#W (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
1: 
1: 	</UL>
1: 	<HR>
1: 	<P>
1: 	<B>SQL State ranges</B>
1: 	<UL>
1: 	<LI>Basic Services
1: 	  <UL>
1: 	  <LI> XBCA CacheService
1: 	  <LI> XBCM ClassManager
1: 	  <LI> XBCX	Cryptography
1: 	  <LI> XBM0	Monitor
0: 	  <LI> XBDA DataComm
1: 	  <LI> XCY0 Properties
1: 	  </UL>
1: 
1: 	<LI>Connectivity
1: 	  <UL>
1: 	  <LI> 08XXX Connection Exceptions
1: 	  </UL>
1: 
1: 
1: 	<LI>Language
1: 	  <UL>
1: 		<LI> 42800-? for compatible DB2 errors
1: 		<LI> 42X00-42Zxx for compilation errors </LI>
1: 		<LI> 43X00-43Yxx  for org.apache.derby.impl.sql.execute.rts
1: 		<LI> 44X00  for all other org.apache.derby.catalog.types
1: 		<LI> 46000  for SQLJ errors (for now, leave this range empty) </LI>
1: 		<LI> 38000  SQL3 ranges  </LI>
1: 		<LI> XD00x  Dependency mgr </LI>
1: 	  <LI> 
1: 	  </UL>
1: 
1: 	<LI>Store
1: 	  <UL>
1: 	  <LI> XSCG0 Conglomerate
1: 	  <LI> XSCH0 Heap
1: 	  </UL>
1: 
1:     <LI>Reserved for IBM Use: XQC00 - XQCZZ
1: 	</UL>
1: */
1:

1: 	** Language

1: 
1: 	/*
1: 	** Language Statement Exception
1: 	*/
1: 	String LSE_COMPILATION_PREFIX="42";
1: 
1: 	/*
1: 	** Language
1: 	**
1: 	** The entries in this file are sorted into groups.  Add your entry
1: 	** to the appropriate group. Language errors are divided into 3 groups:
1: 	** A group for standard SQLExceptions.
1: 	**
1: 	** 428?? - adding some DB2 compatible errors
1: 	** 42X00-42Zxx for compilation errors 
1: 	** 46000  for SQLJ errors (for now, leave this range empty)
1: 	** 38000  SQL3 ranges 
1: 	** 39001  SQL3
1: 	** X0X00-X0Xxx for implementation-defined execution errors.
1: 	**
1: 	** NOTE: If an error can occur during both compilation and execution, then
1: 	** you need 2 different errors.  
1: 	**
1: 	** In addition to the above groups, this file also contains SQLStates
1: 	** for language transaction severity errors. These are in the range
1: 	**
1: 	**	40XC0 - 40XCZ
1: 	**
1: 	** implementation-defined range reserved for class 23 is L01-LZZ
1: 	**
1: 	**
1: 	** Errors that have standard SQLStates
1: 	**
1: 	** Implementation-defined subclasses must begin with a digit from 5 through 9,
1: 	** or a letter from I through Z (capitals only).
1: 	**
1:  	*/
1: 
1: 	/*
1: 	**
1: 	** SQL-J ERRORS -- see jamie for further info
1: 	**
1: 	** DDL
1: 	**	46001 - invalid URL
1: 	**	46002 - invalid JAR name
1: 	**	46003 - invalid class deletion
1: 	**	46004 - invalid JAR name
1: 	** 	46005 - invalid replacement
1: 	** 	46006 - invalid grantee
1: 	** 	46007 - invalid signature
1: 	** 	46008 - invalid method specification
1: 	** 	46009 - invalid REVOKE
1: 	**
1: 	** Execution
1: 	** 	46102 - invalid jar name in path
1: 	** 	46103 - unresolved class name
1: 	** 	0100E - too many result sets
1: 	**	39001 - invalid SQLSTATE
1: 	**	39004 - invalid null value
1: 	**	38000 - uncaught java exception
1: 	**	38mmm - user defined error numbers
1: 	** to be used in the future
1: 	** InvalidNullValue.sqlstate=39004
1: 	*/
1: 
1: 	// WARNINGS (start with 01)
1: 	String LANG_CONSTRAINT_DROPPED									   = "01500";

0:     // 58009 means connection is terminated.  This can be caused by any number
0:     // of reasons, so this SQL State has a lot of instances.
1:     // 
0:     // NOTE: if the disconnection is not caused by DRDA-level error, you should
0:     // use SQL State 08006.  The way I determined this is if the error occurs
0:     // in the 'client.net' package, use 58009.  If it occurs in the 'client.am'
0:     // or any other client package, use 08006.  It's really not at all clear
0:     // from the specs when you should use one SQL state or the other, but that's
0:     // the approach I chose (David Van Couvering).
0:     // Use this version of SOCKET_EXCEPTION any time *except* when trying to
0:     // establish a connection, as the SQLState is different.  When trying
0:     // to establish a connection, use CONNECT_SOCKET_EXCEPTION.

commit:95e7b46
/////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
0: /*
0: 
0:    Licensed Materials - Property of IBM
0:    Cloudscape - Package org.apache.derby.iapi.reference
0:    (C) Copyright IBM Corp. 1999, 2004. All Rights Reserved.
0:    US Government Users Restricted Rights - Use, duplication or
0:    disclosure restricted by GSA ADP Schedule Contract with IBM Corp.
0: 
0:  */
0: 
0: package org.apache.derby.iapi.reference;
0: 
0: 
0: /**
0: 	List of error message identifiers.
0: 	This is the set of message identifiers. The message identifier
0: 	also encodes the SQLState as the first five characters.
0: 	StandardExceptions must be created using the static
0: 	StandardException.newException() method calls, passing in a
0: 	field from this class.
0: 	<BR>
0: 	The five character SQL State is obtained from a StandardException
0: 	using the zero-argument StandardException.getSQLState() method.
0: 	<BR>
0: 	The message identifier (ie. the value that matches a field in this class)
0: 	is obtained using the zero-argument StandardException.getMessageId() method.
0: 	<BR>
0: 	Thus if checking for a specific error using a field from this interface
0: 	the correct code is
0: 	<PRE>
0: 		if (se.getMessageId().equals(SQLState.DEADLOCK))
0: 	</PRE>
0: 	<BR>
0: 	A utility static method StandardException.getSQLState(String messageId)
0: 	exists to convert an field from this class into a five character SQLState.
0: 	<P>
0: 
0: 	<P>
0: 	The SQL state of an error message dictates the error's severity.
0: 	The severity is determined from the first two characters of the
0: 	state if the state is five characters long, otherwise the state
0: 	is expected to be 7 characters long and the last character determines
0: 	the state. If the state is seven characters long then only the first
0: 	five will be seen by the error reporting code and exception.
0: 	<BR>
0: 	If the state is 9 characters long, the last two characters encode
0: 	an exception category, which Synchronization uses to determine whether
0: 	the error causes REFRESH to halt or to simply skip the failed transaction.
0: 	All 5 and 7 character states default to the ENVIRONMENTAL exception
0: 	category.
0: 	<BR>
0: 	Here is the encoding of the SQL state, broken down by severity.
0: 	<UL>
0: 	<LI> <B> SYSTEM_SEVERITY </B>
0: 		xxxxx.M
0: 		
0: 	<LI> <B> DATABASE_SEVERITY </B>
0: 		xxxxx.D
0: 
0: 	<LI> <B> SESSION_SEVERITY </B>
0: 	    08xxx
0: 		xxxxx.C
0: 
0: 	<LI> <B> TRANSACTION_SEVERITY </B>
0: 		40xxx or xxxxx.T
0: 
0: 	<LI> <B> STATEMENT_SEVERITY </B>
0: 		{2,3}xxxx, 42xxx,  07xxx  or xxxxx.S
0: 
0: 	<LI> <B> WARNING_SEVERITY </B>
0: 		01xxx <EM> SQL State rules require that warnings have states starting with 01</EM>
0: 
0: 	<LI> <B> NO_APPLICABLE_SEVERITY </B>
0: 		YYxxx (YY means none of the above) or xxxxx.U
0: 
0: 	<LI> <B> TRANSIENT exception category </B>
0: 		xxxxx.Y#T (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
0: 
0: 	<LI> <B> CONSISTENCY exception category </B>
0: 		xxxxx.Y#C (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
0: 
0: 	<LI> <B> ENVIRONMENTAL exception category (the default)</B>
0: 		xxxxx.Y#E (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
0: 
0: 	<LI> <B> WRAPPED exception category</B>
0: 		xxxxx.Y#W (Y can be any of the preceding severities)
0: 
0: 	</UL>
0: 	<HR>
0: 	<P>
0: 	<B>SQL State ranges</B>
0: 	<UL>
0: 	<LI>Basic Services
0: 	  <UL>
0: 	  <LI> XBCA CacheService
0: 	  <LI> XBCM ClassManager
0: 	  <LI> XBCX	Cryptography
0: 	  <LI> XBM0	Monitor
0: 	  <LI> XBDA DataComm
0: 	  <LI> XCY0 Properties
0: 	  </UL>
0: 
0: 	<LI>Connectivity
0: 	  <UL>
0: 	  <LI> 08XXX Connection Exceptions
0: 	  </UL>
0: 
0: 
0: 	<LI>Language
0: 	  <UL>
0: 		<LI> 42800-? for compatible DB2 errors
0: 		<LI> 42X00-42Zxx for compilation errors </LI>
0: 		<LI> 43X00-43Yxx  for org.apache.derby.impl.sql.execute.rts
0: 		<LI> 44X00  for all other org.apache.derby.catalog.types
0: 		<LI> 46000  for SQLJ errors (for now, leave this range empty) </LI>
0: 		<LI> 38000  SQL3 ranges  </LI>
0: 		<LI> XD00x  Dependency mgr </LI>
0: 	  <LI> 
0: 	  </UL>
0: 
0: 	<LI>Store
0: 	  <UL>
0: 	  <LI> XSCG0 Conglomerate
0: 	  <LI> XSCH0 Heap
0: 	  </UL>
0: 
0:     <LI>Reserved for IBM Use: XQC00 - XQCZZ
0: 	</UL>
0: */
0:

0: 
0: 	/*
0: 	** Language
0: 	**
0: 	** The entries in this file are sorted into groups.  Add your entry
0: 	** to the appropriate group. Language errors are divided into 3 groups:
0: 	** A group for standard SQLExceptions.
0: 	**
0: 	** 428?? - adding some DB2 compatible errors
0: 	** 42X00-42Zxx for compilation errors 
0: 	** 46000  for SQLJ errors (for now, leave this range empty)
0: 	** 38000  SQL3 ranges 
0: 	** 39001  SQL3
0: 	** X0X00-X0Xxx for implementation-defined execution errors.
0: 	**
0: 	** NOTE: If an error can occur during both compilation and execution, then
0: 	** you need 2 different errors.  
0: 	**
0: 	** In addition to the above groups, this file also contains SQLStates
0: 	** for language transaction severity errors. These are in the range
0: 	**
0: 	**	40XC0 - 40XCZ
0: 	**
0: 	** implementation-defined range reserved for class 23 is L01-LZZ
0: 	**
0: 	**
0: 	** Errors that have standard SQLStates
0: 	**
0: 	** Implementation-defined subclasses must begin with a digit from 5 through 9,
0: 	** or a letter from I through Z (capitals only).
0: 	**
0:  	*/
0:

0: 	**

0: 	** Execution

0: 	** 	0100E - too many result sets

0: 	**	39004 - invalid null value
